text:
I have made at least 6 enchilada sauce recipes off this site, even the scratch boil-the-chiles-put-in-blender-strain-etc. This one is not only the easiest, but it's the best. I've made it dozens of times with only a few minor adjustments. At times I use a mixture of New Mexico and Calif chile powders. If I'm out of one, I'll use the other. Both have the best flavor for enchiladas. There doesn't seem to be a reason to use self-rising flour, so I use regular. If I have chicken broth on hand, I use that as a substite for the water. Same with fresh garlic. I add about an ounce or two of dark chocolate to the mix for a bit more depth in flavor. You can't taste the chocolate, but it does add something. 

I dip my corn tortillas in the sauce while the sauce is still pretty hot. I also pour sauce in the bottom of the baking dish before I place the rolled up enchiladas in. Don't worry if your sauce seems too thin; it thickens in the oven.  

Don't bother with any other sauce recipes on this site. Take my word for it, this one is the best.

P.S. The best New Mexico chile powder is the 69 cent "Chile New Mexico Molido" in the red, white, and green package by the company "Mexico Spices Corp"

I hate to give this three stars but I hate it when people rate recipes by the changes they have made.  I followed the recipe exactly and the sauce had way too strong of a chili powder flavor to it, I nearly gaged. So I added more garlic pwd, cumin and onion pwd, it ended up tasting pretty good. However next time I will try 3 TBSP chili pwd and double the rest of the spices. I hope this helps someone! Revised: 04-1-08 I made this again and doubled the spices and only used two TBSP of chili powder it was much better, not perfect but much better.

text:
my family loved this!  I had to make some changes though.  I didn't have tomato sauce, so I blended up a 14 ounce can of tomatoes and juice and used all of it.  It sounded like a whole lot of chile pwdr., and I had no idea what the diffference between New Mexico or Calif chile pwdr., but used what I had and it was great.  I started out using half the amount of chile pwdr. called for just in case and found I needed the entire amount called for.  When it was done, the sauce was a little bland for my taste, so I upped the amount of garlic, onion, cumin to 3/4 tsp.  It was then great!  To this sauce, I added boiled, shredded chicken, (3 boneless skinless chicken breasts) and 2 cans (4 ounce) green chiles.  WOW!!!!   Now we have a very versatile dish!  Use for tacos, enchiladas, salad, nachos-you can't go wrong and I think the end product was a 5 star!  Use your discretion at upping the amount of spice according to your own taste.

text:
I made this last night to put on top of some enchiladas made with homemade tortillas with leftover veggie and meat filling inside. It was delicious! For those who gave it a bad review because of the flour-y taste, the recipe directions state that you should make a roux (pronounced roo) from the oil, flour, and chile powder. This means that you combine those 3 things in a pan with a whisk and let it cook, stirring occasionally, until it is very bubbly and has browned slightly. Then, whisking furiously, you add the rest of the spices and the liquids. This cooks the flour and chile powder first to get rid of that gross floury taste. I followed this recipe to a T, and it was just perfect. I'd definitely make it again.

text:
I think the reviews all depend on what part of the country you are in.  North and Midwestern's may think it's too strong.  Cali folks have their own style just as we have TexMex here in Texas.  

This sauce is fine as a quick sauce.  I did change the order of adding ingredients.  I bloomed ALL of the spices in the oil (I used sunflower oil because it is what I had), then added the flour(I did use white wheat flour).  You have to be VERY careful not to burn the roux.  It is harder to tell the color of the roux because of the spices.  If you even get it a little too brown the sauce will taste BAD and it goes from perfect to BAD in a short time.

The infusion of the spices into the oil is what brings out the depth of flavor (and of course the lightly browned flour).  Skip this step and you will have flat sauce.  Instead of the plain tomato sauce, you may want to try a fire roasted or Rotel canned tomato, throw it in the blender...blend into sauce consistency.  

I had to add about 1/2 tsp salt for my taste.  After I tasted the recipe, I decided to add 3/4 tsp of sugar to it, too - personal preference.

text:
As a native New Mexican, it is law to have a second blender used solely to blend and make the red chile sauce every year (with roasted chiles, water and spices, no tomatoes). The chiles dye the blender dark red-black.    I found that Old El Paso enchilada sauce tastes great and use that instead of slaving away every year.  I felt guilty but every one raves about my enchiladas.  One day I was driving down a county road in Gadsden County, the county that produces all the chile in NM (chile capital of the world) and drove by a huge factory labeled "Old El Paso" on the side. No wonder it taste  great. Made with fresh Hatch chiles in the high dry desert climate of New Mexico.  My review will probably be dropped...but anything that saves time and energy.

text:
My store stopped carrying the brand of suace i usually use, so i made a recipe simmerlier to this, it was pretty darn good but I thought i would try to find something better. This was exellent enchilada sauce, I did add a few squares of hershys choc, and simmered on low for about 20 minutes just to let the spices combine together(Just like i did with my recipe). I actually doubled the recipe and made spanish rice to go along with the enchiladas. Overall a good sauce, very simmilar to what I had already made, so I think next time i will just combine the recipes and see how it turns out. Once you try this though you will never buy canned agian.   Also for those who had a prob with 10 min sauce, simmer it longer, that should fix the prob. Also if you want to make it a day or two ahead of time, that will really let the spices blend together.  Update- the more I make this the better it turns out. I have tried with different types of chili powder and from my experience you need a good chili powder, the cheap stuff just wont do. I have also simmered it for at least 20 minutes.  I still add a few squares of chocolate and add some more garlic and cumin. It is very important to get the oil/flour/chili powder mixture right in order for this sauce to turn out.  *To the reviewer who took the chili powder out... Umm that is what makes it ENCHILADA SAUCE!

I never made enchilada sauce before and was skeptical that this recipe would turn out okay.  I followed the directions exactly and was really pleased with the results.  I bought a roast chicken from the grocery store, cubed it, mixed some of the sauce and some grated monterey jack cheese, then rolled the tortillas in this mixture.  I placed them in a 9X14 pan and poured the sauce over and some more grated cheese and heated it in the over for half an hour.  The result was spectacular, no leftovers.  The only thing I would do in the future is double the recipe if you use a large pan like I did, there just wasn't enough sauce.

text:
I'm an experienced cook, but using the spices I had on hand, it turned out really awful. I buy them in the organic bulk section of a nutrition center, but it's still hard to know how fresh those spices are. So, I rushed out to the grocery store,  made it again, and found the key is using the recommended Chile New Mexico Molido spice and fresh garlic and onion. I found 2-1/2 Tblsp of chili pwdr was plenty, bumped up the cumin and added oregano and garlic salt. It turned out way better with a fresher taste. I didn't give it a five, because I found a reasonably priced canned sauce without additives that tastes very similar to this recipe, and there is no way to make this taste fresh in ten minutes. Flavors have to blend, especially dry spices, so I simmered for 15-20 min. tasting along the way, then let it sit for 10 min. This is a fine base recipe to tweak to your own taste, but use fresh ingredients whenever possible.

text:
Okay Folks, let me tell you that this absolutely the best enchilada sauce I've ever made!  I have lived here in El Paso for over 20 yrs.  This area is known for excellant mexican cuisine, and this recipe is the best of the best!  I've spent years, toasting, roasting, soaking and blending all my fresh ingredients, only to obtain a sauce that was good, but far inferior to this one!  And it really did only take 10 mins.  Add 2 tsp Knorr chicken/tomato powder to soften the chile powder and that's the only change. This is now my secret sauce recipe. (The folks down here would never believe it!)  Don't limit this to using for just enchiladas.  It would also be great for making Chile Colorado, or add a little bittersweet chocolate for a good Chicken Mole!  Very authentic recipe!
P.S. If using regular flour, add 1/4 tps baking soda and a pinch of salt for the self-rising flour.  IMPORTANT NOTE: DO NOT  USE REGULAR CHILI POWDER, USE A GROUND RED CHILE POWDER, IE; NEW MEXICO RED ETC.  IT MAKES A HUGE DIFFERECE IN THE RESULTING FLAVOR!

text:
Quick and easy! Will never buy canned sauce again. One tablespoon of chili powder was plenty for a mild sauce. Don't worry that the oil, chili powder and flour rue seems thin -- it thickens up just fine.  I added more salt and cumin to taste and a dash of unsweetened cocoa powder to bring out the spices.  Made these easy cheese enchiladas:  warm 8 corn tortillas in microwave.  Dip each tortilla fully in sauce, then fill with shredded sharp cheddar and a few canned chopped green chilis. Roll and arrange seam side down in baking dish. Top with more sauce, cheese and chopped green onions. Bake at 350 for 20 minutes until bubbly.

This was okay. The first time I made it, I followed the recipe. The second time, I made changes that improved it, in my opinion. I used 2 tbs. cheapo chili powder and 2 tbs ancho chili powder (which is actually much better than what is originally called for). I skipped the tomato sauce and used a 6-oz can of tomato paste with 1 1/2 c. broth. I doubled the ground cumin, skipped the onion salt (I hate salt) and used double the amount of onion powder and used minced garlic instead of garlic powder. To cut back on the fat, I used 2 tbs olive oil instead of the vegetable oil. I skipped the self-rising (it won't be any more fluffier) and used 4 tsp of all purpose flour. Oh, and I threw in a hint of oregano, just because I could. Yep, definite improvement.

A very fine base sauce, but needs a little tweaking;

why use garlic powder and onion salt, when you can just add fresh minced garlic, finely chopped onions, and then salt to taste?

adding a bit of dark chocolate as mentioned by at least one other reviewer will add a bit more depth that may be lacking in a 10-minute sauce.

chili powder is chili powder, so find one that works for you and roll with it...

I whipped this up for the first time just now, and am quite pleased with the results. Beats canned ANY day. 

Also remember to dip the corn tortillas in the sauce before trying to roll them up, otherwise they'll crack and break, making a frustrating mess...

text:
This was delicious... after quite a few modifications. The ingredient list is a great starting point, but I tweaked the quantities significantly. I began with a 15oz (nearly double recommended) can of tomato sauce as the recipe doesn't yield enough sauce to serve six people well-sauced enchiladas. I used double oil and flour, but kept my New Mexico chili (.69 @ Ralph's) constant at 1/4 cup. I used only 2 c of water. Roughly quadrupled all spices (except salt) and added about a tsp of cocoa powder until the flavor was deeper and more reminiscent of my favorite Mexican restaurant. I simmered the sauce for closer to 20 mins, stirring every couple mins and eventually came out with a nice sauce. Leftovers tasted good too-- sauce holds up well!

text:
Okay, I ended up with a pretty good enchilada sauce but I had to make some big modifications at the end to get there. At first I followed the recipe pretty much as written (the only sub I made was per another reviewer who recommended New Mexico or California Chile powder, and I had both so I went half and half.) I ended up with a very bitter tasting and way too thick mess.

So, I added the following ingredients at the end to help thin it a bit and mellow it out... 1 tbsp sugar, another can of tomato sauce and about another cup and a half of water. I cooked that for awhile on a low simmer and the sauce mellowed into something with a little kick, a good flavor, and the right "saucy" consistency.

As the recipe stands I'll give it 3 stars...but with some improvements it could be 5 stars!!!  Reduce the chili powder (ALL you could taste was chili powder) by at least half and increase the other seasonings according to taste--anywhere from 3/4 tsp. to 1 tsp.

My husband RAVED about this sauce and declared that every Sunday should be Enchilada Day--and all thanks to the sauce!

Four stars as it was good, but not exceptional. Per the other reviewers, I cut down on the amount of chili powder and oil to 3 Tbsp, and upped the cumin, garlic powder, and onion powder to 1/2 tsp. I substituted onion powder for the onion salt, so that I could have more control of the salt. I also let this simmer longer to give it more depth of flavor. 

I'll probably make this again, using more than one variety of chili powder, as it's a little one dimensional with only one type of chili.

I personally did not feel like that was a good recipe. It was "authentic" tasting for simple ingredients, but the tomato sauce over powered the dish and gave it a bland taste if you didn't alter it. I had to change a lot of things and add a lot of extra seasoning in order for it to taste like anything other than tomato sauce. I added brown sugar to round out the flavor of the sauce, and personally I hate cumin so I did a tiny amount and could still taste it. I also used chicken stock instead of water and didn't add flour. I also added Cajun seasoning to give it some more heat and garlic powder to help with depth of flavor.

text:
It's a good BASE recipe to start with.  With mine, I use the full amount of chile powder and add more cumin to it - that, to me, is the real flavor of enchilada sauce.  I also tripled this for a 9" x 13" pan plus a bit left over (great in egg, refried bean, and cheese burritos) and used 2 15oz. cans of tomato sauce and 2 cups water with the amount of oil and flour called for.  I like my sauce on the thicker side so I let it cook about 30 mins.  The real secret to full flavor in mine is that I added 1 packet (or 1 cube) of beef bouillon.  That's really what gave it great depth.

text:
I have gotta say, that this is THE BEST enchilada sauce recipe that I have ever tried and my family agrees. So much better than the canned and so easy to make. Use it with enchilada's made from the pork carnitas recipe at cooking-mexican-recipes.com/pork-carnitas.html and you won't want to have it any other way. Suggest that you have everything pre-measured though because things go pretty quickly once you start. 6 servings is definitely not enough for anything that I cook though, so triple it to be on the safe side and if you want to save some for later, make even more. I usually do 36 servings and put some away for next time.

text:
This is a really good recipe, especially if you are wanting to please lots of people. I would suggest adding a tbsp of cornstarch, mixed with a tbsp of water so it doesnt clump up in the sauce. Also DO NOT use 1/4 cup of powder. Its WAY too much. I used just 2 tbsp and it was perfectly spicy enough, without tasting like lots of chili powder. Also, if you have some, just add about 1 tbsp of taco seasoning. It helps it to taste more authentic and even better than the restuarants. I only gave 4 stars, because without my alterations, thats all that its really worth.

text:
This recipe is so easy, and it's nice to get that little ego boost when you tell people, "I even made the sauce myself" ;) I'll admit that before this, I only used canned sauce, and honestly never even thought about making my own. Then one day I was desperate for a dinner recipe and my available ingredients all added up to enchiladas...except for the lack of sauce. I went on a hunt for a sauce recipe, and luckily I stumbled across the right one the first time! I made a double batch because I only had a 15 oz. can of sauce, used regular flour, and regular McCormick chili powder since it was what I had on hand. Once it was all together I tasted it and thought it was missing a little something, so I added just a splash of lime juice (I like the tang). Other than that, I couldn't be happier! My husband isn't a huge fan of Tex Mex food, but even he said, "Wow, this is really good!" My sons (2 and 4) loved the enchiladas, too. What's really nice, though, is that by making a big batch, I put the extra sauce in a ziplock bag in the freezer for another quick meal. I used the frozen batch yesterday, and it's just as good as when I made it. In the future I'll make a really big batch and freeze it in individual portions, since enchiladas are a new family favorite thanks to this sauce!

I hesitate to rate this recipe because I didn't use all of the right ingredients.  I had Tone's chili powder, not what the recipe called for, and 1/4 cup was way too much. A friend suggested that the bitter taste that resulted could have been from too much cumin, as there is cumin in that chili powder as well as in the recipe. I would make this again but with much less of this chili powder--or with the right kind of chili powder!

text:
Make this a 5-minute enchilada sauce. Try whipping it up in the microwave! Heat your oil about one minute on high in a microwave bowl big enough for the whole batch of sauce. Add flour (I used all purpose) and chili powder. Stir it all up until there are no lumps. Heat it for about 1 minute more on high, stirring once at the 30 second mark, to â€œbrownâ€ mixture. It gets thick and the chili powder made mine quite dark brown from the start. Add water, tomato sauce, spices. Stir it all into the chili powder/ flour roux, thinning it. Heat it on high for about 3 minutes more, stirring once at midpoint. Voila, (or is that Ole?) youâ€™ve got a great red sauce, slightly thickened like you want. I made mine ahead. I refrigerated it, then reheated it to assemble my enchiladas. So easy and tasty. No more canned sauce for me!

text:
I thought that using self-rising flour and browning the chili powder with the roux might account for the slight off taste that other reviewers mentioned.  I used Wondra instant mix flour.  As soon as the flour/oil mix was lightly browned, I removed the pan from the heat and whisked in the chili powder and other spices.  After the water and tomato sauce were added, I returned it to the heat and let it cook until slightly thick.  I only had half the required amount of chili powder on hand, but it was still very nicely spiced.  We thought it had excellent flavor and was far superior to canned or packaged enchilada sauce.  It was very easy to make and used items I always have in my pantry.  Thanks for sharing your recipe!!

text:
I tried this recipe tonight because I only had one small can of sauce and I had 5 grandchildren visiting and my husband's brother. My husband found this recipe. I have never tried to make enchilada sauce but thought sure I will give it a try. When I read the recipe I thought 1/4 cup of chili powder sounded like a lot of chili - my husband told me that many of those that rated it mentioned that they cut the chili amount in half - so that is what I did. I didn't have the self rising flour either and never use it - I used regular flour and it worked just fine. I don't know if my chili powder was Calif. or Mexico but it tasted just fine too. I had cooked a beef roast in a slow cooker and that is the meat I used for the enchiladas. I used the meat juice in place of the 1 1/2 cups of water. Often I cook chicken or pork this way for enchiladas too; I have decided I will use this recipe again and keep using the juice of whatever meat I cook instead of the water. Next time however, I will use fresh garlic instead of the powder. I love fresh garlic but I had 5 hungry children and I had started dinner later than I had expected - so to save time I used powdered garlic. 
The kids "loved" the enchiladas, I was getting a bit worried I was not going to get any. My brother in law loved the sauce too as did my husband. So it looks like I won't be buying canned sauce anymore. Oh, I used pureed tomato sauce instead of regular tomato sauce because that is all I had on hand.

text:
This is a great base sauce. Following some reviews (and also based on what i had on hand) i came up with the best version for my family. From the get go, I didn't have flour so i substituted 1 tbsp cornstarch. I only had a regular chile powder so i used a dash of that. I used a 15 oz can of tomato sauce and 1 cup water. Then, i had old el paso original taco seasoning so i used 1 heaping tbsp of that along with a dash of cumin and half a tsp crushed jarred garlic. I also used a touch of lime juice and 1/4 cup mini chocolate chips, which gave it a great creamy consistency without a chocolatey flavor (tasted creamy and as if there was a touch of cocoa). I let simmer on lowest heat for about 20 mins before adding a little bit more of the taco seasoning and lime juice. It was incredible.

Freshly ground sea salt, freshly ground pepper, simmered x 15 minutes, and I created a very tasty sauce.

text:
Mmmmm... this was really excellent! I made this recipe because I accidentally bought 'medium' enchilada sauce at the store, and DH can't stand spicy food. I made a few changes based on what I had to work with, and it was really wonderful. I used olive oil (don't keep veg. in the house), less chili powder (about 3/4 of what recipe called for - family preference), and I made tom. sauce by heating 8 oz of water, and adding tomato paste a bit at a time until it had the right flavor/consistency (about 3/4 of a 6oz can)I let that simmer while I made the rest of the recipe. Also, added chicken bouillon to 1c water called for and heated before adding to recipe. I didn't add salt because of the bouillon. At the very end, I threw in 5 hershey kisses dark chocolate because I had 5 left... The end result was something I will continue to make. My husband loved the addition of the chocolate - it added a bit a sweetness and depth to the flavor. The sauce was nice and thick, and had beautiful color. This was fun and easy to make, even with the changes - Thank you for the great recipe!

text:
I wanted to try the recipe as is, and I really didn't like it, so I started over following a lot of the other suggestions.  I sauteed a half an onion, a small hot pepper, and a clove of garlic in about 2 tbsp of oil, then added the flour to that mixture.  From there I added a 15 oz can of tomato sauce and equal parts cumin, garlic powder and chili powder plus some salt and pepper.  I also added some dark chocolate at the end.  This turned out fantastic and I will never buy canned sauce again.

I used homemade chicken stock because I had it in place of the water.  I added 1 C of water per recipe for a double batch.  I had fresh chili powder so reduced it by 1/3 and added some dark chocolate coco powder.  Tweaked spices for taste.

As someone said, the important step is not over doing the spices and flour in the oil but allowing them to cook through before adding the tomato sauce etc.

This is a great recipe and quite fast.  I think the idea is that you can make it quickly but it will probably taste even better after the flavors have a chance to blend.  It is great because it uses things you should have on hand.  

Thank you for sharing.  I used it tonight for chicken enchiladas and my DH who loves Mexican food really liked it.

text:
I made it nearly exact to Brandi's recipe.  This was an outstanding sauce, way way superior to the standard bright red stuff served at most Tex-Mex restaurants.  I suppose how good it is depends on the quality of your chili powder! Some have complained of lack of depth to their sauce.  I used Frontier brand organic chili powder. The method of browning your flour in fat is making a roux. If you let this spice-oil mix brown properly and gradually it will create plenty of flavor with depth!!  Next time I would consider adding Chipotle powder for smokiness and intensity. Maybe 1 Tbsp of coffee for more depth too (it does amazing things to chili).

text:
This was so easy when you are short on time and don't have any enchilada sauce on hand.  I use regular chili powder (2 Tbsp.) and about 2 Tbsp. of raw chopped onions and a dash of salt in place of the onion salt because I did not have the ingredients called for by the recipe on hand.  I will likely continue to use raw onions in the sauce when I make it again.  They were tasty in the sauce.  I added the cumin and garlic sauce to taste, a little heavier on the cumin.  Super easy and the spices are flexible to taste.  Will definitely use again, no need to buy a jar of sauce.

text:
I have to admit, I am not exactly sure what plain enchilada sauce is supposed to taste like.  I have a recipe that calls for 1 can of enchilada sauce and realized last-minute that I didn't have any.  Thankful to find this recipe!  I dialed down the chili powder since my kids won't eat anything if it's too spicy.  I doubled the recipe (to use 1 15-oz can of tomato sauce) and started with 1/4 cup of chili powder.  At the end, I added another Tablespoon - I probably could've added a bit more, but I think 1/2 cup would've been too much.  I also used chicken broth instead of water because I had some in the fridge that I needed to use up.  I wasn't sure how it was going to work, but I used it in my recipe and my husband said he liked the recipe better than before, so there you go - homemade is best :)  And boy did it make a lot of sauce!  I only needed 10 oz so I am going to portion out the rest and freeze for next time!  No more store-bought cans of enchilada sauce - good stuff.

country:
None
text:
This was my first attempt at making homemade enchilada sauce. I followed the recipe exactly, but ended up adding oregano after tasting, as it seemed flat to me. I wish I'd used broth as others had done, but adding 1/2 tsp of oregano and simmering a bit longer seemed to improve it (thankfully, I made this way in advance of assembling the enchiladas).  It's a simple recipe that I will keep, but next time will use broth instead, and add oregano with the other spices.

Also, when you add flour and chili powder together, you cannot tell when the flour is browned, because it's the color of chocolate right at the start. I waited and stirred until I was sure the raw flour taste would be gone, but I've made a ton of roux in my lifetime, and felt comfortable that it had browned enough.  Next time I will follow the advice of another reviewer and start with your oil/flour and add the chili powder once the flour has browned.

text:
This sauce is wonderful. I always get compliments, and it's dramatically cheaper (and better!) than than the canned stuff if you do it right. I buy a big can of tomato sauce (105 ounces) from Costco for $3. I buy all my seasonings in bulk, so even the incredible amount of chili powder (2 cups) necessary for this recipe is under $1. I made chicken stock with Better than Boillion (12 cups of water for this amount), so that's also cheap. All in all, under $5 for 6-32 oz canning jars full of Enchilada (plus some extra!). If the store bought stuff actually was better, I would buy it. But really, this stuff is better. I even use basic chili powder, nothing special (sadly, I'm sure it's better with the recommended kinds but I cannot find them to save my life). I do add about twice as much of the other recommended seasonings, and I make a roux with the flour and oil to begin with (then when it is properly browned, I add chili powder, stir rigorously for about a minute and add remaining ingredients). After this, I simmer it for as long as I can. This time it was about two hours. Longer would have been better, but as is, it's great. There is a taste to canned Enchilada sauce that bothers me. This, obviously, does not have that taste. To adjust the ingredients for a 105 ounce can of tomato sauce, just multiply everything by 8. Fully recommend!

text:
wonderful basic recipe to "bounce " off of! My changes were as follows:  I started with a homemade broth that was made with skin and bones of turkey. the broth had been made the day previously and the fat had risen to the top. when I made my roux, i also added all the fat from the broth.  yes, use all of that chili powder! but be careful that your chili powder isn't already mixed with salt.  look at the ingredients! i ruined chili once as a young cook because i didn't know some chili powder is "cut" with salt.  On the same subject, I didn't add any additional salt because my enchilada recipe was gonna be salty already, and you can always add more salt later!   anyway,  I quadrupled the recipe ( prolly?) and added some cornstarch to help thicken it some.  I knew it would be fantastic and time consuming, so i made enough for 1 pan of enchiladas and then froze 3 ziplock bags of sauce for future recipes.[ { 1) add cocoa powder to enchilada sauce and you have mole sauce to cook with chicken! 2) wonderful addition to a pot of chili 3) more enchiladas!! }]This was  absolutely wonderful! Also, i used a huge jar of tomato paste, and added fresh garlic to it all. Lastly, in agreement with so many, the secret to a good sauce is a long slow simmer. yes, you can serve it in 10 minutes and that is fine, but I had the time today to start with a very watery sauce that I brought to a rolling  boil and then  let simmer for 1-2 hours ( i didn't time it) and it was outstanding. text:
This is another "go to" recipe for me.
I used chicken stock instead of water.  The stock was made from two roasted chicken carcasses.  I also used half New Mexico and half California ground chili....El Guapo, the brand you get at Mexican grocery stores (Mojave is another good brand)  Since another cook complained about the strong chili taste I made it a point to throughly cook the chili/flour roux, making sure everything was well cooked...no off tastes, no bitterness.   The finished sauce was great, one of the best I have made

text:
We like things a little saucy here at my house so this recipe served as a base to my own adaptation.  No offensive of course but have just came up with my own sauce that is adequate with what my family of five  enjoys.  I start off my putting my tomato sauce in a pot (50 oz.) then I just add the idegediatnts listed in the respice omitting the oil & flour rue ( I did this because ounce the sauce and spices where in the pot it was pretty thick as is.  Next I simmered it and "melded" the flavors together in hearty sauce. lastly I added 2 T. of sugar and 1/2 cup of water (still simmering for a 5 min. stirring after a minute or so)  This is the 2nd time I have made it my way and it's turned out fabulous each time. Credit to the original recipe for giving me that base that I was unclear of once starting out!!!  ***By the way my recipe made 10 enchiladas, dipped and rolled and set in a casserole dish lined in the sauce and smoothed on top of them as well before adding cheddar cheese***

text:
This recipe is great! Enchiladas and fajitas are the only Mexican foods I like and this is spot-on. However, living in a small town in Florida, it is hard to find specialty spices, so I used 1/2t cayenne powder and 1/2t chipotle powder, I also prefer fresh garlic over powdered, so I used 3 cloves. These make it restaurant quality and still very spicy due to potencies. I have also added a dash of cinnamon and 1t cocoa powder and that gives it a deeper flavor, more may make it even better. The amount of water is a good amount as it should be cooked for a while to fully infuse flavors and cook the flour. I gave four stars due to not using the original recipe.

text:
I haven't bought ready made sauce since finding this!  It is excellent as posted, but I do change it up sometimes, depending on how much time I have:   I use broth instead of water, either chicken or beef, depending on what kind of meat I'm using in the enchiladas.  Sometimes I'll use chopped onions and garlic rather than the powders:  salute them.in oil, add the rest of the spices and salute a minute or so more, stirring them into the onion mix.  If you want a thicker sauce, now is a good time to stir in a tablespoon or so of flour, then slowly add everything else.    I make this in big batches, then freeze in print containers for use later.  Excellent sauce.

I didn't have another 8 oz. can of tomato sauce so I used some 'squeeze' tomato paste.  I kept squeezing til it tasted like 'tomato'.  I also put 1/4 teas. of cinnamon for a little extra boost.  I used Wondra flour (love it).
I let it simmer for about 45 min. while I gathered the rest of the items needed.  When I served it up he was amazed and declared it was the BEST enchilada sauce he'd ever tasted.  That's a big deal cause he eats lots of Mexican food here in the southwest.  So I had to write it all down for the next time I make it.  It's so simple and delicious.

WOW!!!! We will never go back to a store bought mix. I was concerned about the amount of chili powder being too hot for my wife. It's not! The spices blend wonderfully and the sauce is easy (fast) to prepare.

text:
I rarely review something here, but wished to do it on this recipe. I read many reviews before making it. Here's what I did: 1) I used 2 T Mexican chili powder (from Santa Fe School of Cooking) -- not enough!! Next time I will add at least another 1 T more and perhaps a pinch of cayenne. This comes from someone who doesn't like a lot of heat. 2) I only used low-med heat for the oil, chili powder and flour. There's low risk to burn this at this heat level. 3) I doubled the recipe, but next time I would TRIPLE it. I had standard-sized tortillas and doubling the recipe wasn't enough. When doubling the recipe I did NOT add in water or broth, so it was nice & thick.  I also used minced garlic and to use up some shallots, I sauteed 5 chopped-up shallots. I used an enchilada recipe from W-S. Hope some find this helpful.

I wanted to make Chicken Enchiladas for supper, but I forgot to buy salsa (even though it was on the list) so I figured we could use an Enchilada Sauce in place of it, for that tomatoe-y element. text:
I made it in 10 minutes and gave it depth. Brown flour in skillet in advance until deep golden brown and keep it handy in a jar (keeps for up to a year.  Use high quality beef broth instead of water. Use highest quality chili powders you can acquire (I use several fresh blends that I buy in bulk at the health food store), use lard, not vegetable oil. Talk about depth.  Mexicans use lard, not veg oil. It gives the depth that butter would. Add fresh garlic and fresh ground cumin.  If you have all these things on hand, it's no problem. I didn't use any tomato's at all!

country:

text:
I followed the original recipe, except I used onion powder, rather than onion salt and didn't add any salt. I tasted it and it was not good, at all. WAY too much chili powder and it was really bitter. The sauce was really dark. I think the issue is the chili powder. I added another can of tomato sauce, 1/4 tsp cumin, 1/4 tsp onion powder. 1/2 tsp garlic powder, 1 and 1/2 cups of water, 1/2 tsp oregano, 1/2 tsp of paprika, 1/4 tsp cinnamon, 1/4 tsp ground cloves, 1 tbsp of rice wine vinegar and 1/2 tsp of sugar, to cut the bitterness. Left it on medium simmer while I made my filling, grated cheese, etc. Approx. 20 minutes to let the flavors, meld. It made a thicker sauce than I expected and really coated my white corn tortillas. I believe it reduced by a quarter, to a third. I used 2/3 of the sauce for 8 beef enchiladas in a 9x13 baking dish. I won't use *this* recipe again.

I prefer lots of sauce for dishes like enchilada, so I doubled the recipe.  I thought 1/4 cup chili pwdr was A LOT for even a double batch, so I decided to use only 1/4 cup (1/2 of what I 'should have' used)  Even then I thought the sauce was a bit too strong...I am SO GLAD that I didn't add more. Overall this his is a good basic recipe. I did make minor modifications:  1) used 1 TBSP of All purpose flour. (Adding 2 will make the sauce too thick; more of a paste consistency rather than a sauce)   2) added 1 tsp of cumin to give it more of a mexican flavor.   3) I did not have New mex chili powder so used regular chili powder.  4) Used homemade chicken broth instead of water (use beef stock or broth if making beef enchiladas)

text:
Overall, this sauce was good.  It is super easy, and doesn't use a ton of ingredients which is why I chose this one.  I can't say it's that much better than store bought enchilada sauce, but it was good.  I was concerned about the amount of chili powder at first, that seemed like alot so I thought maybe it was an error or it was going to be super spicy, but nope, it's right.  I had to make this sauce twice because the first time it burned right after I added the chili powder.  The second time it came close, but I took it off the heat when I was adding the chili powder though.  I'm not counting off for that because I was using a stove I'm not use to, and different stoves/ovens heat differently so that would probably explain the ruined first batch - just watch your heat when adding the chili powder!

text:
I used 1 C of beef broth instead of the water. 2 T of chili and doubled the other spices. I also omitted the oil altogether. This made it good but I am giving it only 3 stars since I changed so much. Mine already had a pinch too much chili powder so I can't imagine using as much as the recipe says.  To make the easiest enchiladas, I use hamburger helper's cheesy enchilada and cook as per package instructions. I roll this into tortilla shells and place in a baking pan, pour this on top, dump a lot of pre-shredded cheese on top and bake for 5 min and broil for another 2 min. Serve with shredded lettuce and for those that want, jalapeno peppers and sour cream. Very easy.

text:
I used tomato paste instead of flour to thicken... which meant I had to simmer it for much longer. I took the extra time I had to grate the cheese & chop onions for the cheese enchiladas I used the sauce for. I stuck mostly to the recipe using the onion salt & garlic powder, as I don't like chunky sauce (I put the fresh stuff in the enchiladas themselves). I tried the New Mexico chili powder as suggested (whole amount) & it wasn't too hot at all. In fact, next time I think I will try 1/2 NM & 1/2 CA to make it a little spicier. I did substitute chicken broth for water & added the chocolate as some reviews had suggested, & it seemed to give it a nice extra touch. Make sure if you add chocolate to use a dark chocolate w/ about 50%-60% cacao, NOT unsweeted 100% cacao. I though this was a great starter recipe, especially if you have never made this type of sauce before, or if you are on a time constraint.

text:
I found myself without any enchilada sauce, yet all set to make them.  When, once again, AllRecipes comes to my rescue.  This recipe is soooooo good!  I had a 29 oz. can of tomato sauce sitting around, so used that and tripled the rest of the recipe.  I used regular flour, and just kept adding water until I liked the consistency.  I let it simmer while I prepared the rest of the ingredients--this time I used ground beef. I also mixed in some of the sauce with my meat and onions (and sometimes I add black beans with the meat), which made them very good.  At the table I got 3 votes--1 too spicy, 1 too un-spicy, and 1 just right.  By making so much sauce, I was able to make an extra pan of enchiladas to freeze for later, and had a big container to freeze, so I'll have sauce for the next time I want to make enchiladas!!  Thanks, Brandi.
